Wish I could give no stars - please read previous recent reviewers Becca Jones-Starr, Della Moran and others because my story is EXACTLY the same.

I also was told I had periodontal disease, among other things and was shown a $6000 bill while sitting in the dental chair. I knew I couldn't afford that, but when I was told the minimal amount of treatment needed was ONLY $900 it sounded like they were offering me a bargain. I also was told my insurance would not cover the cost of the type of cleaning I needed, but a Perio Tray I could use at home would at least "heal my gums". I ONLY CAME IN FOR A CLEANING AND ROUTINE CHECK because I had recently moved away from my old dentist! I felt totally railroaded.

They also asked if I had a Care Credit Card and had I not said that I already had one, they probably would have had me apply for one! It should be noted that Care Credit is a high interest card that can be useful if you qualify for a no-interest promotional period and can pay it off in 6 months or so. It is the type of credit arrangement that can get you into debt if you're not careful, but providers like Western Dental like it because they get their money upfront.

On top of that, the dentist came back in and asked me to give a review of her assistant WHILE I WAS STILL SITTING IN THE CHAIR! She asked me if I had a phone, got it out of my purse, took it out of my hand and showed me the review app. I clicked 3 stars because I thought I was rating the nice-ness of the assistant and the doctor then said no, no I needed to give 5 stars so her assistant could get a free lunch. HOW UNPROFESSIONAL IS THAT?! I was clear-headed enough to skip the review, but they got over $900 out of my HSA.

After I walked out of the office I came to my senses and walked back in to say I had changed my mind about the Perio Tray. Sorry, they said, the molds they took had already been sent off to a lab and they couldn't "pull the ticket". What??? How does a tray get sent off that fast??? After pushing the issue, the office manager said she would TRY to refund me half of the money, but it would have to be approved by the main office. Needless to say, since last June I have been trying to get some money back that was taken from my HSA to no avail because Western Dental must have great legal advisors who write up their scam policies.

At this point, I would just like the $425 refund they offered but never delivered on. I certainly will never set foot in there again and am warning others! YOU WILL NOT SAVE ANY MONEY by going to Western Dental nor will you feel like you are listened to and cared for.<//Text>

The doctors are great. The staff are fantastic. I have no complaints about the quality of the treatment I got.

However this place exemplifies everything wrong with the American Healthcare system. In the waiting room (which you will have to spend plenty of time in - more on that later) I never had one wait where there wasn't someone poor or elderly or both having an issue with their insurance provider and the bureaucratic nightmare it places everyone in.

About those wait times. What on earth is the point of this place even pretending to schedule appointments? If you schedule me for 1:30; and I'm not seeing a doctor until past 2:45, this is NOT an appointment. I've never had an appointment here that started when it was scheduled and I've had the unfortunate circumstance of having  5 'appointments' with them in the past two weeks. Every time I end up waiting for hours and hours.

Clearly the staff are over worked and overbooked. They do great work still in their facilities that seem laughably outdated.

Bottom line, if you can find somewhere else that's better do it. Even if it's an hour drive or more do it, because you'd probably still save time rather than going to this place. If you must come here though just don't schedule anything else on your calendar for the rest of the day. Seriously like block out the next 3-4 hours, you'll be waiting for a long time.< /review>

<Rate>4<//Rate><text>Second time here and have been very happy with the service and food.

The okonomiyaki will be delivered to you already made on a hot metal plate so it will keep it nice and warm.

The seafood one is pretty stuffed with goodies as well as the beef one (their specialty). Others, I couldn't really taste the ingredients, alas they were all delicious.

Appetizers as well as other dishes were really good as well. Specially the tsukemen, the sauce was flavourful and spicy. In contrast to other tsukemen I had, the sauce was cold and noodles were hot (freshly boiled). All ingredients (meat, veggies, etc.) were in noodle bowl.

I would recommend this place to try out if you are craving some okonomiyaki and want to try out some bomb tsukemen.<//text>< pictures>

<user>102153220420411626109< /user><Name>Amy Lloyd<//Name><time>1559243651155</time><Rate>4< /Rate>< review>
Chinchikurin (DTLA) has been on my radar for a while now because, shockingly, there aren't a lot of places to get Okonomiyaki in SoCal. The bf and I were just doing some errands in the South Bay and were looking for some dinner on Yelp and Chinchikurin popped up! We were really excited to be so close to one since we've been wanting to try it.

The Hiroshima style Okonomiyaki is the specialty here and I believe the difference is that there is noodle in the Hiroshima style. There are so many different types to choose from so we decided to try the classic one with the pork belly and fried squid and the Chinchikurinyaki, which has ground beef. You can also choose between soft or crunchy noodles so we gave both a try. The classic okonomiyaki tasted great and very authentic. You definitely want to add some Japanese mayonnaise on top of this one; it makes all the difference! The Chinchikurinyaki was very different and new to me, but it was delicious! It is very meaty compared to the pork belly which is good for the bf lol.

The restaurant was quite small. If anyone is familiar with the Torrance area, this place took over what used to be Musha. I expect this restaurant to be very packed once it gets more hyped up. I'd definitely come back to try other things on the menu.<//review>

< review>
Ambiance: small packed okonomiyaki place, usually long waiting list during the weekend

Service: very friendly though a bit forgetful, it took long to get water served

Food: simple items on the menu, choices of soft or crispy noodles
The Hiroshima - **** known as one of the most popular dishes in Hiroshima, this dish includes ikaten inside of the okonomiyaki and is topped off with green onions, very flavorful, recommend
Spicy Tan Tan Men - **** soupless spicy noodles, could choose spicy level from 1 to 4, slightly spicy and contains sansho, this dish contains a hearty portion of noodles topped with ground pork, negi, and a sprinkle of togarashi, the special mixing broth contains a variety of oil and spices, rich in flavors, recommend

Price: decent portions and prices, about $20 per person< /review>

< Review>
Hiroshima-style Okonomiyaki, the best I have had outside of Japan. Okonomiyaki is a super flavorful cabbage-noodle-egg pancake, cooked on a hibachi type flattop, and topped with a rich sauce. Fillings range from pork to ground beef, with the Hiroshima specialty ikaten (fried squid) a really tasty and highly recommended choice. Vegetarian choices are also delicious.
Plenty of tables for parties of 4 or more, but if you sit at the bar you can watch the Okonomiyaki being made in front of you.
There is usually a wait after 6 or so on weekends, so plan accordingly.<//Review>

< Review>
The first time i came here food was good. But not this time.... The place is small and had to wait not much. I got the molcajete ranchero that has carne asada, chorizo, pollo, queso, nopales, cebollitas, arroz y frijol. And a salad. Tbh everything was without sabor. I was extremely dissatisfied especially because it was pricy. Around 15$ for that plate. My friend got the fajitas with shrimp and carne asada. Same ...had no flavor. The only stars i gave is due to the guacamole we ordered. It was really good. And another star for the waters. We got horchata and jamaica & they were pretty good. Sometimes norte√±o/musicos walk in the restaurant and you pay them if you want to hear a song. I thought that was pretty cool. But the food sucked. Maybe because it was Sunday and it was more crowded than last time I came.</Review>
